<div id="review_2015609074" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015609074" />
    <a title="Trent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19885276-trent"><img alt="Trent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601477767p2/19885276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015609074?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trent" href="/user/show/19885276-trent">Trent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19885276-trent?shelf=memory-sorrow-and-thorn">memory-sorrow-and-thorn</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015609074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7324101061950980776">I love this book and series, and consider it an all-time classic that belongs in the company of LotR, ASOIAF, and the other Fantasy greats. <br/><br/>That said, I do want to break down the things I liked and disliked from The Dragonbone Chair: <br/><br/>- The beginning of the book is slow, and then even after it begins to 'pick up', there are still pacing issues. I wasn't overly bothered by it, but I can definitely see how it could be a barrier to some readers. It's hard for me to think of too many other books I ha</span>
  <span id="freeText7324101061950980776" style="display:none">I love this book and series, and consider it an all-time classic that belongs in the company of LotR, ASOIAF, and the other Fantasy greats. <br /><br />That said, I do want to break down the things I liked and disliked from The Dragonbone Chair: <br /><br />- The beginning of the book is slow, and then even after it begins to 'pick up', there are still pacing issues. I wasn't overly bothered by it, but I can definitely see how it could be a barrier to some readers. It's hard for me to think of too many other books I have read (other than maybe some by Robin Hobb) that have started this slowly - though still confidently.<br /><br />- The world-building is not always clear. There are a lot of names in this book, and they don't always click super easily. It took me a while (and frankly, I'm still not totally clear) to get my head around some of these names, places, and history. I would have loved for there to be a solid Wiki like you find for ASOIAF, Malazan, WoT, etc.<br /><br />Now let's talk about where the book succeeds, IMO:<br /><br />- The writing. My god, the writing. I feel like I've never really heard /read anyone discuss Tad William's prose before, but dear lord does he deserve to be in the same category as Hobb, Rothfuss, GGK, and the other wordsmiths in Fantasy. His skill in prose and description is honestly what kept me going, even when the pacing was a bit too slow. Just an absolute joy to read, while still being totally approachable for readers of all ages.<br /><br />- The characters also stand out, particularly Simon. I can see why some readers might be annoyed by him, but I really grew to love him - even more than comparable characters like FitzChivalry Farseer or Kvothe. I loved how fallible he was, but also how he perseveres and grows. He's so earnest that's it's impossible *not* to love him, IMO. I enjoyed many of the side characters as well - Marya, Binabak, Josua, etc. <br /><br />- The lore and history, while confusing at times, was still very well thought out and had me yearning to learn more. I love that it feels almost like it's ripped out of our history - there are even hints of a Christianity-like religion. It just feels like there is a lot more to be learned below the surface, which I really love.<br /><br />Overall, this was a great read - particularly when you look at in the context of when it came out, preceding Wheel of Time, ASOIAF, Realm of the Elderlings, and other modern Fantasy giants. It feels almost like the beginning of modern Fantasy, in many ways. Definitely worth your time, and highly recommended. I can't wait to start The Stone of Farewell!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7324101061950980776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_469622693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469622693" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469622693?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=used-books">used-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=here-be-dragons">here-be-dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469622693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14434111730063062319">Oh, the orphan boy with unknown talents, who under-performs until the pressure is applied—how many fantasy stories have you read with this structure? Let’s see--<i>Magic’s Pawn</i> by Mercedes Lackey, <i>The Riftwar Saga</i> by Raymond Feist, <i>The Belgariad</i> by David Eddings, <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> by Terry Brooks, even to some extent <i>The Hobbit</i> and <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> by Tolkien (substitute “hobbit” for “boy”). Maybe even the King Arthur story to some extent—until young Arthur pulls the sword from the stone. </span>
  <span id="freeText14434111730063062319" style="display:none">Oh, the orphan boy with unknown talents, who under-performs until the pressure is applied—how many fantasy stories have you read with this structure? Let’s see--<i>Magic’s Pawn</i> by Mercedes Lackey, <i>The Riftwar Saga</i> by Raymond Feist, <i>The Belgariad</i> by David Eddings, <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> by Terry Brooks, even to some extent <i>The Hobbit</i> and <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> by Tolkien (substitute “hobbit” for “boy”). Maybe even the King Arthur story to some extent—until young Arthur pulls the sword from the stone. It’s a well-used idea.<br /><br />At the book’s beginning, I found Simon particularly annoying. As lives go in Midieval-like settings, his lot in life isn’t so bad, although the housekeeper Rachel does make his existence somewhat miserable. However, we all have to earn our keep, so pull up your socks, laddie, and make an effort! Even when offered opportunities to learn to read and to study, he complains! Typical 14-year-old, I guess, something I wouldn’t know about, having had the reading bug ever since I learned to read. Simon doesn’t appreciate his warm bed, three square meals a day, and secure surroundings until he has to flee the castle.<br /><br />Once he starts running for his life, Simon begins growing up. He becomes a much more likeable character at that point and I began to get invested in his tale. He loses some of the ADHD qualities that made him a “mooncalf” in the beginning and becomes a much more focused young man.<br />I also appreciated a brand new take on trolls—making them smaller, wiser, and wilier. I liked Binobik and his wolf companion a lot. The Sithi are interesting in their ambiguity—are they enlightened, ethereal beings like the elves in Tolkien? Or are they the dark enemies of mankind? The world of Osten Ard is very detailed and easy to picture in the mind’s eye. <br /><br />The writing isn’t the best ever, but the story is engaging and I am waiting impatiently for volume 2 at my public library, where it is ‘on order.’ No telling how long I will have to pause before I know what happens to Simon, the kingdom, and the Storm King!<br /><br />Book number 239 in my Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy reading project.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14434111730063062319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135466777" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135466777" />
    <a title="Crperry13" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3924822-crperry13"><img alt="Crperry13" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135466777?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crperry13" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crperry13" href="/user/show/3924822-crperry13">Crperry13</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Patient people who don't care about dialog.</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135466777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10742601276655320837">My introduction to Tad Williams was the Otherland quartet, which rank among the very best books I ever read. Otherland had strong characters, an engaging plot, and a fast-paced movielike quality about it. I expected the same from other Williams works, so I picked up The Dragonbone Chair for some summer vacation reading.<br/><br/>And I was incredibly disappointed. The utter lack of engaging dialog and prevalence of weak, forgettable characters ruins this book. I found myself flipping past 2-3 pages at a ti</span>
  <span id="freeText10742601276655320837" style="display:none">My introduction to Tad Williams was the Otherland quartet, which rank among the very best books I ever read. Otherland had strong characters, an engaging plot, and a fast-paced movielike quality about it. I expected the same from other Williams works, so I picked up The Dragonbone Chair for some summer vacation reading.<br /><br />And I was incredibly disappointed. The utter lack of engaging dialog and prevalence of weak, forgettable characters ruins this book. I found myself flipping past 2-3 pages at a time of tedious descriptions of scenery, clothing, weather, and emotions to get to the few lines of dialog per chapter. Not that I have any real issue with description - my favorite books are detailed explorations of fantastic ideas or places (check my list!). But this book was tedious...it could have been 200 pages shorter and a much more engaging story, without cutting out one line of dialog. I don't like giving up on books, but after 250 pages of this one, I quit on it and picked up something a little less frustrating.<br /><br />Brutally disappointing. I still want to read Williams' later works (post-Otherland), but am less enthused.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10742601276655320837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26829117?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/954784-lori">Lori</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26829117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17011489232094854886">I love this series. I hadn't thought of it in a little while, but speaking about books today with a friend brought it to mind and I thought, "I haven't read that this year...I should." The four LARGE volumes are quite an investment, both in money and in time, (get it from the library, or let me know and you can borrow mine when I'm done) but it's worth it in the end. I know that sci-fi/fantasy are seriously formulaic, and these are not that different...young boy, thrown into circumstances beyond</span>
  <span id="freeText17011489232094854886" style="display:none">I love this series. I hadn't thought of it in a little while, but speaking about books today with a friend brought it to mind and I thought, "I haven't read that this year...I should." The four LARGE volumes are quite an investment, both in money and in time, (get it from the library, or let me know and you can borrow mine when I'm done) but it's worth it in the end. I know that sci-fi/fantasy are seriously formulaic, and these are not that different...young boy, thrown into circumstances beyond his control, rises to win friends and influence people and then defeats the ultimate enemy and finds true love...blah blah blah...but I so enjoy this particular telling. I still see the country and the people in this series so clearly in my mind. The friends become people you want to meet, and the evil is described in ways that make you realize that even fantasy has a basis in the reality of our crazy world. (Knowing about the evil out there by keeping up to date with the world is different than "throwing your door open and letting whatever evil passes by to come in. It is much more difficult to make that evil leave again.") Besides you know a book like this has entered your heart when you end with the thought that, "I want to name a son Simon after a hero like him!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="17011489232094854886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=warfare">warfare</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer326388898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16345116071119590118">Out of the older tradition of fantasy writing, this one takes its time and builds slowly, carefully, meticulously, until we have a world and conflict that feels real and surprising in the present with the depth that a long history provides. Really good stuff if you're patient enough to let it simmer. <br/><br/>I will admit to being bored at times, and frustrated with Simon's ignorance and naivete, especially in this first book. What I would consider to be the introduction takes about 200 pages. Then it's </span>
  <span id="freeText16345116071119590118" style="display:none">Out of the older tradition of fantasy writing, this one takes its time and builds slowly, carefully, meticulously, until we have a world and conflict that feels real and surprising in the present with the depth that a long history provides. Really good stuff if you're patient enough to let it simmer. <br /><br />I will admit to being bored at times, and frustrated with Simon's ignorance and naivete, especially in this first book. What I would consider to be the introduction takes about 200 pages. Then it's not really until the end of this book that it really reaches the pace and depth that spurs you on to pick up the rest - immediately. <br /><br />No, it's not your quick fantasy fix, but it's infinitely more satisfying than the easy-in, easy-out fantasies that abound these days. I've now read the series twice in spite of the slow start, so I feel that it merits a place on my favorites shelf.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_124258160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124258160" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124258160?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780886773847" href="/book/show/317449.The_Dragonbone_Chair">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=wizardy-magic">wizardy-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=series-that-are-finished">series-that-are-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124258160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18435936670980523690">What a fantastic story. Some people can't stand special snowflake Simon, but I love it all.<br/><br/><i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> is takes a long time to build, and therefore it's hard to give a spoiler free premise. Our main character is Simon, a young orphan boy living in the Hayholt castle. He is a dreamer, someone unfit for the dreary castle life. When he becomes the apprentice of the fascinating Morgenes, he feels like he might finally become part of the adventures and grand life he has always fantasized abo</span>
  <span id="freeText18435936670980523690" style="display:none">What a fantastic story. Some people can't stand special snowflake Simon, but I love it all.<br /><br /><i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> is takes a long time to build, and therefore it's hard to give a spoiler free premise. Our main character is Simon, a young orphan boy living in the Hayholt castle. He is a dreamer, someone unfit for the dreary castle life. When he becomes the apprentice of the fascinating Morgenes, he feels like he might finally become part of the adventures and grand life he has always fantasized about. However, he doesn't know that he will become part of a journey that isn't nearly as glorious as he expected it to be.<br /><br />In many ways, <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> is a classic fantasy story. Simon as special snowflake-y as they come - there is no denying it. However, I love following his development from a naive scullery boy to a responsible young man. Simon is a dreamer, an idealist, which is something I can relate to. He develops from someone that things happen to, to someone who becomes more in control of his own fate. He finds bravery, friendship, and through hardship loses his naiveté. His is a typical coming of age story, but a heartfelt one.<br /><br />The world of Osten Ard slowly unfolds like a scroll being opened. When Simon is young, our perspective is limited to the capitol. As Simon's scope broadens, so does ours. We learn more about the different tribes inhabiting Osten Ard, and the tensions between them. Instead of dumping this whole world on the reader at once, we're being taught its mythology piece by piece. There is a lot of background to learn, and I would not call the book a fast-paced one, but I feel all the background adds to the story. The scope of the book is truly epic, and without the sense of history the world building provides, the whole book would fall flat. <br /><br /><i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> is published in 1988, and its story might no longer appeal to the modern sentiments of contemporary fantasy lovers. If you're looking for a classic story with clear Tolkienesque influences, give <i>The Dragonbone Chair</i> a try. A good fantasy story is timeless after all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18435936670980523690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1136881801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1136881801" />
    <a title="Monica Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11497566-monica-davis"><img alt="Monica Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351746311p2/11497566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1136881801?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica Davis" href="/user/show/11497566-monica-davis">Monica Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11497566-monica-davis?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11497566-monica-davis?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1136881801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17111926464860266252">4.5 stars, deservedly rounded up to 5 stars for the overall enjoyment of this first book in the "Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn" series. A slow start and one or two sections in which I was lulled into near boredom (hence the missing half star in the rating), but beyond that a great adventure filled with interesting, well developed characters; colorfully descriptive and imaginative places and things...and plenty of action and intrigue once the story gets going. The author's careful attention to painti</span>
  <span id="freeText17111926464860266252" style="display:none">4.5 stars, deservedly rounded up to 5 stars for the overall enjoyment of this first book in the "Memory, Sorrow, and Thorn" series. A slow start and one or two sections in which I was lulled into near boredom (hence the missing half star in the rating), but beyond that a great adventure filled with interesting, well developed characters; colorfully descriptive and imaginative places and things...and plenty of action and intrigue once the story gets going. The author's careful attention to painting a scene is remarkably well done, and consistent throughout the book. Character interaction is also well crafted. Looking forward to continuing on with this series.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vdphEJsnbhtKydTT7Apk3HV1EWY7zhSlmDD+ISp01NuPzdyKIrduGIvRZPR56QreIJDFrL+TpAmLYRGpzsJVRg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eHGeAO4b7ZSZmVMcvtDKz1HonDfLeSxAmu/Tv25mUgZKZiOaV4vtl1iB4zsrM6TNBA1I/U8knOyJvjw3itDTmw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer160084209012303953">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an</span>
  <span id="freeText160084209012303953" style="display:none">Tad Williams is a California-based fantasy superstar. His genre-creating (and genre-busting) books have sold tens of millions worldwide, in twenty-five languages. His considerable output of epic fantasy and science fiction book-series, stories of all kinds, urban fantasy novels, comics, scripts, etc., have strongly influenced a generation of writers: the ‘Otherland’ epic relaunches June 2018 as an MMO on steam.com. Tad is currently immersed in the creation of ‘The Last King of Osten Ard’, planned as a trilogy with two intermediary novels. He, his family and his animals live in the Santa Cruz mountains in a suitably strange and beautiful house. @tadwilliams @mrstad</span>
